<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_49355ac0-c2a1-45c7-b425-4f8f3e2ffb3a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText868518486913039746" style="display:none"><p>
  <b>The stunning, massively bestselling story of Napoleon's first fiancé</b>
</p> <p>First published in 1953, this riveting true-life tale comes to life in diary form, giving readers an inside glimpse at the young Napoleon and his family. Désirée is enchanted by the young officer, and he asks her to marry him. But he must leave for Paris, where he meets his eventual wife Josephine. A heartbroken Désirée is unsure she'll ever find anyone again. A love story, but so much more, <i>Désirée </i>is the tale of a simple merchant's daughter who ends up with a kind of royalty she never expected: an unforgettable story just waiting to be reborn.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1884729859516111720">Désirée =	Desiree, Annemarie Selinko<br/><br/>Eugénie Bernardine Désirée Clary (8 November 1777 – 17 December 1860), in Swedish officially Eugenia Bernhardina Desideria, was Queen of Sweden and Norway as the consort of King Charles XIV John (a former French General and founder of the House of Bernadotte), mother of Oscar I, and one-time fiancée of Napoleon Bonaparte. She officially changed her name there to Desideria, which she did not use herself.<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه نوامبر سال 2005میلادی<br/><br/>عنوان: دزیره؛</span>

بهرام رحیمی نژاد؛ تهران، ایران جوان، 1389، در 719ص؛ شابک 9786005798159؛<br /><br />مترجم: آرا جواهری؛ تهران، نگارستان کتاب، 1390، در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره دوجلدی 9786001900457؛ <br /><br />مترجم: کیوان عبیدی آشتیانی؛ تهران، افق، 1391، در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره دوجلدی 9789643697266؛ چاپ دیگر 1393؛<br /><br />مترجم: مژگان فامیلی؛ تهران، لیدا، 1393، در 664ص؛ شابک 9786006267968؛<br /><br />مترجم: ترمه شادان؛ تهران، هنر پارینه، 1394، در 720ص؛ شابک 9786005981704؛ <br /><br />مترجم: پرویز شهدی؛ تهران، مجید، صدای معاصر، 1387، در 775ص؛ شابک 9789644530876؛ چاپ چهارم 1392؛<br /><br />مترجم: مرضیه صادقی زاده؛ تهران، آسو، 1394؛ در 816ص؛ شابک 9786007228609؛<br /><br />مترجم: عطیه بنی اسدی؛ تهران، یاقوت کویر، 1395، در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره دوجلدی: 9786008191049؛<br /><br />دزیره اثری ست از «آن ماری سلینکو»، که ماجرای زندگی «دزیره کلاری»، همسر «کارل چهاردهم»، و مادر «اسکار اول» را، از زبان خودش شرح می‌دهد، ماجراها در زمان ناپلئون بناپارت است و ...؛<br /><br />چکیده داستان: داستان از آنجا آغاز میشود که برادر «ناپلئون» در زمانیکه او تنها یک سرباز ساده بود، با خواهر «دزیره» ازدواج میکند، و از آن پس، «دزیره کلاری» و «ناپلئون» به هم دل میبندند، و پس از مدتها نامزد هم میشوند؛ از این دلبستگی زمانی نمیگذرد تا اینکه پس از دو سال «ناپلئون» نامزدی خود را به هم میزند، و علیرغم؛ قول و قرارهای خود، با دختر دیگری ازدواج میکند؛ بدعهدی «ناپلئون» دل «دزیره» را میشکند او در نامه ای به «ناپلئون» مینویسده: «تو زندگی مرا به سوی بدبختی هدایت کردی اما من هنوز هم راهی برای فراموش کردن تو نمیبینم!»؛ «دزیدریا» یا همان «فرانسیس کلاری» پس از به هم خوردن نامزدیش با «ناپلئون» با ژنرال «ژان باتیست برنادوت» ازدواج میکند و از اینجا داستان به سمت و سوی جذابتری سوق داده میشود؛<br /><br />نمونه هایی از متن ترجمه جناب پزشکزاد: (لحظه هایی از تاریخ هیچگاه از عشق خالی نبوده است و آنگاه که عشق به تاریخ ورود پیدا میکند تاریخ رنگ و بوی تازه ای به خود میگیرد و شوری دیگر میانگیزد<br /><br />بناپارت نماد قدرت طلبی عهدشکنی و برتری جویی است و عشق این صفات را برنمیتابد و آنگاه که معشوق همه هستی خویش را در قمار عشق به تمنا نهاده است ناکام میماند تا خود را به دست مرگ بسپارد و دست قدرتمند عشقی دیگر او را از میان اندوه و رنج میرهاند و به زندگی تازه ای فرا میخواند که سراسر مهر است و عشق و دلبستگی! دستانی که از آستین ژنرال دیگری برون آمده تا مهر بورزد و نوازش بخشد. ژنرال فرانسوی که به سوئد دعوت میشود و تاج پادشاهی بر سر مینهد<br /><br />و آنگاه که دزیره در اوج شکوه در مقام ملکه سوئد در کنار همسر خویش است. آن ژنرال جوان دیروز در هم شکسته و خرد در جزیره آلپ روزهای تبعید را پشت سر میگذارد و اینگونه است که تاریخ پیمان شکنی عشق را روایت میکند<br /><br />حقوق انسانی لغو شدنی نیست! هر چند که ممکن است پاره ای موقتاً آشکارا یا در نهان آن را زیر پا بگذارد و لگدمال نمایند. اما کسانی که چنین میکنند بیگمان مرتکب بزرگترین و خونبارترین جنایات شده اند و در هیچ کجا و هیچ زمانی هیچ کس حق طلب بخشایش برای یغماگران آزادی و برابری برادران خود را نخواهد داشت<br /><br />لحظه ای با خود اندیشیدم که چه خانواده وحشتناکی هستند اما بیدرنگ از این فکر خود شرمنده و خجل شدم چرا که گناه فقر و پرشماری افراد خانواده را نمیباید به گردن تک تک آنان انداخت و اینکه به سبب تنگدستی اتاق نشیمنی جز آشپزخانه نداشتند گناهی نابخشودنی به شمار نمیآمد<br /><br />تاریخ بشر مجموعه ای از سرنوشتهای افراد است، تنها مردانی که عهده دار امضای احکام و فرامین هستند و از بهترین و کارامدترین شیوه های کاربرد توپها آگاهند و میدانند چه وقت و چگونه آنها را آتش کنند، سرنوشت جهان را نمیسازند، به گمان من دیگر مردمان نیز از شمار بنیادگران تاریخ بشریتند؛ تمامی مردان و زنانی که آماج گلوله قرار میگیرند و یا سرهاشان از پیکرهاشان جدا میگردد؛ تمام آنانی که امیدوارانه زندگی میکنند، عشق میروزند و سرانجام میمیرند، سازندگان تاریخ بشری هستند.)؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 09/07/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382322356?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cordula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cordula" href="/user/show/10958654-cordula">Cordula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382322356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer215602283654380896">Maybe this book is not a literary masterpiece, but its pages have become like old friends over time.<br/><br/>When I was a teenager this book was passed on to me by my mother, who had also read it when she was my age. The pages are now littered with the teenage dreams of two generations, I guess.<br/><br/>At the heart of this novel stands one of the lesser known love stories of the 18/19th Century, that of young Désirée Clary who falls desperately in love with dashing soldier Napoleone Buonaparte. But when Napoléon</span>
  <span id="freeText215602283654380896" style="display:none">Maybe this book is not a literary masterpiece, but its pages have become like old friends over time.<br /><br />When I was a teenager this book was passed on to me by my mother, who had also read it when she was my age. The pages are now littered with the teenage dreams of two generations, I guess.<br /><br />At the heart of this novel stands one of the lesser known love stories of the 18/19th Century, that of young Désirée Clary who falls desperately in love with dashing soldier Napoleone Buonaparte. But when Napoléon, as he will become known, leaves her for Paris and the charms of one Joséphine, Désirée's journey only just begins. <br /><br />Spoilers ahead, but only if you're not a history buff...<br /><br />While her and Napoléon's paths recross through the years, Désirée falls in love with one of the Emperors generals, who will end up becoming the Swedish king - Jean-Baptiste Bernadotte. The Swedish royals to this day carry the name Bernadotte...<br /><br />The book has its cheesy moments, undoubtedly. But it does tell a real story, albeit with some embellishment on the side. But what would a historical novel be without it?<br /><br />Told as a diary, we read Désirée's deepest secrets and watch as she grows from impatient teenager, waiting for her life to begin, to wife, mother, crown-princess and queen.<br /><br />I have read this book many times. For many it will probably not deserve a five-star rating. But I can open my old copy, which is almost falling apart at this point, anywhere and just read on. I know this book, inside and out. And that alone is part of its charm...</span>
  <a data-text-id="215602283654380896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_121834931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121834931" />
    <a title="Margaret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162759-margaret"><img alt="Margaret" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234732285p2/162759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121834931?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/162759-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688014483" href="/book/show/1398459.D_sir_e">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=authors-qrs">authors-qrs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=napoleon">napoleon</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121834931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3120055940561966269"><i>Désirée</i> is one of those old family favorites which I've read many times and keep coming back to like an old friend. <br/><br/>It's the sweeping story of Désirée Clary, the daughter of a Marseilles silk merchant, from her early love for and engagement to Napoleon to her later marriage to French Marshal Jean-Baptiste Bernadotte, who later became king of Sweden (and Désirée queen). Désirée herself is one of its chief charms; as the book is in the form of an ongoing journal, everything is filtered through her</span>
  <span id="freeText3120055940561966269" style="display:none"><i>Désirée</i> is one of those old family favorites which I've read many times and keep coming back to like an old friend. <br /><br />It's the sweeping story of Désirée Clary, the daughter of a Marseilles silk merchant, from her early love for and engagement to Napoleon to her later marriage to French Marshal Jean-Baptiste Bernadotte, who later became king of Sweden (and Désirée queen). Désirée herself is one of its chief charms; as the book is in the form of an ongoing journal, everything is filtered through her sparkling, direct, and charming personality. <br /><br />Historically, I find it largely convincing (though I'd still like to read a good biography of Bernadotte to see if her picture of him is accurate), particularly in the portrayal of Napoleon, who can easily turn into a caricature of himself if handled wrongly; Selinko makes him entirely believable, as an egotistical tyrant, but also as a human being. Although Désirée marries Bernadotte, it's her scenes with Napoleon which are frequently the most arresting and emotional.<br /><br />If you've read <i>Désirée</i> and are interested in a historical diarist of that time, I'd highly recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5605175.Memoirs_Of_The_Duchess_D_Abrantes__Madame_Junot_V7__1835_" title="Memoirs Of The Duchess D'Abrantes, Madame Junot V7 (1835) by Laure Junot" rel="nofollow noopener">Memoirs Of The Duchess D'Abrantes, Madame Junot V7</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3120055940561966269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5929641?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne" href="/user/show/291160-susanne">Susanne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783462031027" href="/book/show/99666.D_sir_e">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical fiction lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291160-susanne?shelf=historicalfiction">historicalfiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5929641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3712090863047789983">The bad first - it is fictional and it is basically chick-lit. But seriously...one of the best historical fiction/chick lit books.<br/><br/>The novel tells in diary style the life of Désirée Clary-Bernadotte. Napoleon Bonaparte's first fiancee, later Madame Marechale Bernadotte and finally Queen Desideria of Sweden (who is also sister-in-law to Napoleon's brother Joseph). All of these are true historical facts and make in themselves a compelling read. In her diary entries which run from about 1793 to 1830</span>
  <span id="freeText3712090863047789983" style="display:none">The bad first - it is fictional and it is basically chick-lit. But seriously...one of the best historical fiction/chick lit books.<br /><br />The novel tells in diary style the life of Désirée Clary-Bernadotte. Napoleon Bonaparte's first fiancee, later Madame Marechale Bernadotte and finally Queen Desideria of Sweden (who is also sister-in-law to Napoleon's brother Joseph). All of these are true historical facts and make in themselves a compelling read. In her diary entries which run from about 1793 to 1830, she describes in detail the events of the late French Revolution and Napoleon's power, but there is always the personal aspect of a woman who supports the Revolution, loves her husband, her son and her family beyond anything and fears for their wellfare and safety.<br />It is a lovestory (somewhere in there), it is historical and it is incredibly entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3712090863047789983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49376583" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49376583" />
    <a title="Misfit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit"><img alt="Misfit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496595931p2/1375548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49376583?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misfit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misfit" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit">Misfit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=one-time-read-only">one-time-read-only</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=get-it-from-the-library">get-it-from-the-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=napoleon">napoleon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=france">france</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49376583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3929737593523651814">But for the fact that she went to get her brother out of jail....<br/><br/>Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, a wealthy silk merchant's daughter, would not have met young impoverished Napoleon Bonaparte and how different her life might have been. Enchanted by the young officer, she invites him and his brother Joseph to her home - where Joseph finds himself attracted to her sister Julie and her very generous dowry. Still too young to wed at fourteen, she and Napoleon are engaged, but the older Joséphine de </span>
  <span id="freeText3929737593523651814" style="display:none">But for the fact that she went to get her brother out of jail....<br /><br />Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, a wealthy silk merchant's daughter, would not have met young impoverished Napoleon Bonaparte and how different her life might have been. Enchanted by the young officer, she invites him and his brother Joseph to her home - where Joseph finds himself attracted to her sister Julie and her very generous dowry. Still too young to wed at fourteen, she and Napoleon are engaged, but the older Joséphine de Beauharnais has something to say about that. Although heartbroken, Désirée recovers and eventually marries French General Jean-Baptiste Bernadotte, although he spends much of their marriage away from Paris in service to the now Emperor of France. Eventually Bernadotte is nominated to become Crown Prince of Sweden, and subsequently King with Désirée as its reluctant Queen. <br /><br />Written in diary format from Désirée's POV, her story give the reader an inside glimpse at the young Napoleon and his family, through his opulent days as Emperor lavishing gifts and titles on his family, on to his final defeat at Waterloo. As interesting as much of this history was, I found myself snoozing off at times as the author lost me with a too busy cast of characters, too many of which were always called "your royal highness" and nothing else that I had a hard time following who was who. Worse yet, the diary format really painted the author into quite a corner and she had a hard time getting herself out of it at times - frankly she fell out of that corner on more than one occasion. Writing in your diary and you quote verbatim a long long letter from your son? I don't think so. If you're a big fan of anything and everything Napoleonic and want to read more I'd go for it, but definitely not for a first time reader of this period in France's history. 3/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3929737593523651814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92304486" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92304486" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900147-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544395177p2/900147.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92304486?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/900147-laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Wanda, Jeannette, Virginie</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laura by: </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92304486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7326777048208351097">This is the story of Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, he daughter of François Clary, a wealthy silk manufacturer and merchant, and his second wife, Françoise Rose Somis. Her sister, Julie Clary, married Joseph Bonaparte, and later became Queen of Naples and Spain.<br/><br/><img alt='' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242154.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Eugénie was introduced to Napoleon Bonaparte by his brother, Joseph Bonaparte who met her by chance when she was trying to release her brother Etienne, who was arrested in her father's place by the revolutionary authorities. It was Nap</span>
  <span id="freeText7326777048208351097" style="display:none">This is the story of Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, he daughter of François Clary, a wealthy silk manufacturer and merchant, and his second wife, Françoise Rose Somis. Her sister, Julie Clary, married Joseph Bonaparte, and later became Queen of Naples and Spain.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242154.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eugénie was introduced to Napoleon Bonaparte by his brother, Joseph Bonaparte who met her by chance when she was trying to release her brother Etienne, who was arrested in her father's place by the revolutionary authorities. It was Napoleon who suggested that Joseph should become engaged to her older sister Julie instead, while he should be engaged to Désirée. In less than a year, Napoleon met Joséphine de Beauharnais and broke his engagement with Eugénie.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242155.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Désirée moved to Paris in order to live with her sister and her brother-in-law, she received a marriage proposal by Coronel Junot. She then met and married Jean Baptiste Jules Bernadotte, another French general. <br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242156.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The author magnificently describes Désirée's life through her diaries which were addressed to her father and which were written since she was fourteen years old.<br><br>It was amazing to learn how a daughter of a simple silk merchant of Marseilles became engaged to Napoleon Bonaparte, married Jean Baptiste Jules Bernadotte - Charles XIV John, king of Sweden and Norway, and then became Queen Desideria of Sweden and Norway.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242157.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Page 137:	 <br>"As long as we had General Bonaparte in Italy we won all the battles and the Austrians begged for peace. As soon as he's away to carry our glory overseas everything is upside down.' Strange, the impression Napoleon's campaign has made on simple people."<br><br>Page 220:	 <br>"A movement of startled surprise went through the ranks of spectators. Napoleon had broken the pre-arranged crowing ritual and had crowned himself!<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242158.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Page 298:<br>"Your Royal Highness," the young man continued, "as a Chief Chamberlain of His Majesty King Charles XIII of Sweden I beg to report that the Parliament of Sweden has unanimously elected the Prince of Ponte Corvo to be Heir to the Throne. His Majesty King Charles XIII wishes to adopt the Prince of Ponte Corvo and to welcome him in Sweden as his beloved son."<br><br>Page 418:<br>Napoleon himself was at Fontainebleau with 5,000 men of his Guards regiments. Caulaincourt negotiated for him with the victors. On April 4th (1814) he signed his declaration of abdication.<br><br>A movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0046903/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Désirée (1954)</a> was made based on this book, with the unforgettable actors Marlon Brando, Jean Simmons, Merle Oberon and Michael Rennie.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397172311i/9242159._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review92304486">

<div id="review_283668150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283668150" />
    <a title="Amalie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4164661-amalie"><img alt="Amalie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600148509p2/4164661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283668150?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalie " href="/user/show/4164661-amalie">Amalie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4164661-amalie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4164661-amalie?shelf=scandinavian">scandinavian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283668150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11212157286441132248">I got this book from the library for my mother who enjoys these historical romance novels but I also ended up reading it. For those of you who can read German, it's better to check out the original version of the book, though I have no complains about this translation, I'm sure that is even better.<br/><br/>This is written in diary format from Désirée's (Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, who later becomes the Queen of Sweden and Norway) POV. <br/>Here's a picture of her: <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370756i/723652.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She is one-time fiancée of Napoleon Bon</span>
  <span id="freeText11212157286441132248" style="display:none">I got this book from the library for my mother who enjoys these historical romance novels but I also ended up reading it. For those of you who can read German, it's better to check out the original version of the book, though I have no complains about this translation, I'm sure that is even better.<br><br>This is written in diary format from Désirée's (Bernardine Eugénie Désirée Clary, who later becomes the Queen of Sweden and Norway) POV. <br>Here's a picture of her: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370756i/723652.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She is one-time fiancée of Napoleon Bonaparte who he dumps for Josephine. One should not think this is the story of Napoleon Bonaparte, this is very much her story. It gives the reader an inside glimpse at the young Napoleon and his family, his days as the Emperor and on to his final defeat at Waterloo. <br><br>From what I understood Napoleon choose Josephine over her is because of wealth but he continues to have a strong bond with her. And I just noticed how these dictatorial men don't seemed to have had a love life: Hitler, Napoleon, Lord Voldemort... I think if he had married Désirée there might never would have been a French Revolution! Then the wars, invasions... the bad stuff BUT THEN, the great books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24280.Les_Mis_rables" title="Les Misérables by Victor Hugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Misérables</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/656.War_and_Peace" title="War and Peace by Leo Tolstoy" rel="nofollow noopener">War and Peace</a> would have never been born. Bummer! Irony! Irony! ;P<br> <br>This is really a novel that is likely to be enjoyed more by female readers. There are certain places melodramatic but then you learn they really happened, I wonder perhaps little exaggerated? For an example: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Napoleon leaves Desiree for Josephine, she wants to throw herself off a bridge, but is waylaid by a tall, handsome gentleman who she eventually marries who becomes King Charles XIV John of Sweden. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And you thought these things happen only in romance novels!! <br><br>*Recommended for historical fiction lovers. <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11212157286441132248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120661294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120661294" />
    <a title="Amy Bruno" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1774372-amy-bruno"><img alt="Amy Bruno" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493316012p2/1774372.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120661294?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Bruno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Bruno" href="/user/show/1774372-amy-bruno">Amy Bruno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402244025" href="/book/show/7854269-d-sir-e">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=france">france</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=napoleon">napoleon</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120661294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7145340280095254505">In his memoirs, dictated while he was in exile on the island of St. Helena, Napoleon named his first love as Desiree Clary, a silk merchant’s daughter from Marseilles. In the breathtaking novel simply titled Desiree, author Annemarie Selinko chronicles the life of the woman who was Napoleon’s fiancee, a woman who rose from being a commoner to becoming a wife of a General to Queen of Sweden and Norway. <br/> <br/>As a little girl Desiree received a diary from her beloved father and through it she narrates </span>
  <span id="freeText7145340280095254505" style="display:none">In his memoirs, dictated while he was in exile on the island of St. Helena, Napoleon named his first love as Desiree Clary, a silk merchant’s daughter from Marseilles. In the breathtaking novel simply titled Desiree, author Annemarie Selinko chronicles the life of the woman who was Napoleon’s fiancee, a woman who rose from being a commoner to becoming a wife of a General to Queen of Sweden and Norway. <br /> <br />As a little girl Desiree received a diary from her beloved father and through it she narrates her story. Desiree first meets Napoleon through his brother Joseph, who will later become her brother-in-law, and takes a fancy to the young and determined General. Even though their relationship would die young and he would break her heart, Napoleon and Desiree would remain in each other’s lives until his quest for world domination ended in his exile to St. Helena. <br /><br />Desiree is a mesmerizing look at the rise and fall of Napoleon told from the woman who first held his heart and knew him like no other. It is touching and beautifully written and no historical fiction readers’ library is complete without this exceptional, un-put-down-able novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7145340280095254505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3643684?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynette" href="/user/show/228942-lynette">Lynette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/1589218.D_sir_e">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3643684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16961062031567688435">Excellent older book by Annemarie Selinko about the life of Eugenie Desiree Clary, a silk merchant's daughter, who was the first love of Napoleon Bonaparte. She later married Jean Baptiste Bernadotte who became the King of Sweden. Their descendants rule Sweden today.<br/><br/>I read this book years ago and am rereading it again. The only criticism I have is that the book becomes bogged down at times with the information about Napoleon's campaigns and the political landscape of the time. Important informat</span>
  <span id="freeText16961062031567688435" style="display:none">Excellent older book by Annemarie Selinko about the life of Eugenie Desiree Clary, a silk merchant's daughter, who was the first love of Napoleon Bonaparte. She later married Jean Baptiste Bernadotte who became the King of Sweden. Their descendants rule Sweden today.<br /><br />I read this book years ago and am rereading it again. The only criticism I have is that the book becomes bogged down at times with the information about Napoleon's campaigns and the political landscape of the time. Important information but also tedious. <br /><br />Desiree is an engaging and charming character, but portrayed as a rather simple and uneducated young woman, lacking in some of the social graces. However, she seemed quite adept at capturing the hearts of two very important and influential men despite her middle class upbringing and lack of education. The one thing that did bother me throughout the whole novel was Bernadotte's calling her "little girl" as an endearment. Perhaps he actually called her that but I found it annoying after a few times.<br /><br />Overall, an entertaining read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16961062031567688435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17961350650739281755" style="display:none">I just wrote a long review and it somehow disappeared. what did I do wrong? I loved this book. It is old, copyright 1953. It was one of the first books I read when I came into this country from Germany. <div id="review_1938340085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1938340085" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373481234p2/4784586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1938340085?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24058420-desiree">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=heroine-too-stupid-to-live">heroine-too-stupid-to-live</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1938340085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13748333633268053245">This used to be one of my favorite books back when I was a teenager, but reading it again after all this time, I can't for the life of me figure out why. I don't know if it's the diary style, the translation, or if I've just changed very drastically since then. <br/>But honestly, I couldn't stand Désirée this time around. I thought she was childish (and since pretty much every man she interacts with, including her husband, tells her all the time how childish and stupid she is, I guess it can't be jus</span>
  <span id="freeText13748333633268053245" style="display:none">This used to be one of my favorite books back when I was a teenager, but reading it again after all this time, I can't for the life of me figure out why. I don't know if it's the diary style, the translation, or if I've just changed very drastically since then. <br />But honestly, I couldn't stand Désirée this time around. I thought she was childish (and since pretty much every man she interacts with, including her husband, tells her all the time how childish and stupid she is, I guess it can't be just me), and her refusal to learn anything new that might help her navigate in her new surroundings while complaining how no one likes just annoyed me until I couldn't take it anymore. <br />But the last straw? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Désirée's husband is elected heir to the Swedish throne, and knowing that he will never amount to anything under Napoleon, he accepts and re-locates his family there. Désirée does not feel like preparing for this new role (why bother with learning about their etiquette, culture, or language?), complains all the time about having to live in a palace, and hates the climate (guess what, it's cold up there. Who could've known…), and then feels sorry for herself because no one there likes her. I wonder why…. After a few months of not trying to fit it, she decides the best thing for her husband and young son is for her to move back to France, which is where she lost all my respect for good. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Also, I don't find the love triangle particularly romantic. To me, it felt like Jean-Baptiste only wanted Désirée because she used to "belong" to Napoleon (and because and he could save her from killing herself after Napoleon dumped her), and little Désirée being completely oblivious to their little competition was just painful. <br />The second star is pure nostalgia, for all those fond memories of the days where I would curl up on the couch and lose myself in the story. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13748333633268053245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_302464487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302464487" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2628389-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332772679p2/2628389.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302464487?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/2628389-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302464487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9447162041712955170"><br/>Annemarie Selinko's last novel: Desiree has become my top favourite 18th c HF read- without a doubt. The story of Eugenie Desiree Clary, Napoleon Bonaparte's first love is in my opinion one of the best novels ever written pertaining to the Revolution era- in terms of history, romance, historical characters, and impeccable writing style. This book kept me captivated from beginning to end. And- the funny thing is that I read this intermittently due to other priorities, so I naturally thought I'd f</span>
  <span id="freeText9447162041712955170" style="display:none"><br />Annemarie Selinko's last novel: Desiree has become my top favourite 18th c HF read- without a doubt. The story of Eugenie Desiree Clary, Napoleon Bonaparte's first love is in my opinion one of the best novels ever written pertaining to the Revolution era- in terms of history, romance, historical characters, and impeccable writing style. This book kept me captivated from beginning to end. And- the funny thing is that I read this intermittently due to other priorities, so I naturally thought I'd for sure lose momentum and interest. This never happened and when I finally finished the book, I almost felt the parting sadness when losing a dear friend.<br /><br />The story begins with Desiree writing the story of her life through a journal given to her by her father, prior to his death. The daughter of a fabric merchant, Desiree, was unpretentious, straight forward and incredibly brave and loyal in love, honour, friendship and family. Her strength of character (even when she didn't feel quite up to it...) was incredible. From the very beginning we can see her determination when it came to saving the raggedy young Napoleon at the beginning of his career. I loved reading about their romance and meager beginnings...all the short way upto his unfaithfulness and hurtful betrayal to leave Desiree for Josephine. This though, would not be the end of their encounters.<br /><br />Throughout their lives, Desiree would always play an important role in Napoleon's life-not amorously, but with extended family and politically. Her attachment to the Bonaparte family, by the marriage of Napoleon's brother to Desiree's sister- and politically through her husband's (Bernardotte) importance (he first fought along Bonaparte's side and then became the King of Sweden). The history is impeccable and the story told with the perfect blend of simplicity and grandiose royal style (yes, it's possible).<br /><br />I loved that Desiree's life entertwined Josephine's and her family- along with all the Bonaparte's and other significant historical characters (Fouche, for one). The novel takes us through their lives as well, giving a different perspective- and not just passing glimpses. But, most definitely, what I loved the most was the way Desiree always stood up to Napoleon. We encounter moments of truthful courage where Desiree speaks her opinion frankly and keeps her head high- even though she is terrified inside...others would have surely perished at the hands of Bonaparte for this behaviour- but not Desiree. This too showed us a side of Napoleon that remained loyal and respectful of the bond and young love they once shared. The book is filled with precious moments.<br /><br />And what more of this brave girl...Desiree becomes part of Royalty herself; so for those who don't really know that part of history, I won't spoil it for you. I could go on forever about this book: Desire's regular-girl-achieving-great-things personality, her love for her husband, the King of Sweden, Bonaparte's wins and defeats, Josephine's other side, the Bonaparte family, Desiree's business and Royal side, the losses, the pain, the trials and triumphs and some of the funniest moments as well...It's all just too good.<br /><br />Desiree is a spectacular book, and I HIGHLY recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9447162041712955170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1548021630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548021630" />
    <a title="Dani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2335986-dani"><img alt="Dani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380636142p2/2335986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1548021630?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/2335986-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1548021630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3005005011507044243">A really nice read for lovers of historical fiction. Yes, this is what "Désirée" is: It teaches you something about history, but there are also many fictional relations and details. I liked it mainly for two reasons: because I learned a new perspective of this part of the European history and because it was told from the view of a woman who didn't care much about politics and became involved in it anyway. I sympathized with the main character and with her struggles. <br/><br/>Last year, I read another nov</span>
  <span id="freeText3005005011507044243" style="display:none">A really nice read for lovers of historical fiction. Yes, this is what "Désirée" is: It teaches you something about history, but there are also many fictional relations and details. I liked it mainly for two reasons: because I learned a new perspective of this part of the European history and because it was told from the view of a woman who didn't care much about politics and became involved in it anyway. I sympathized with the main character and with her struggles. <br /><br />Last year, I read another novel about this era - "War and Peace" by Tolstoy. It was really interesting to get to know the other side, the way the French thought and acted. If I have to compare the two books, I have to admit that Tolstoy managed to develop more sophisticated characters. But this acknowledged, "Désirée" also presents some intriguing personalities like Josephine, Bernadotte or Napoleon. They are really neither black nor white, they are rather lively characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3005005011507044243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13465570568070412745">My mother was reading this book when she was pregnant with me. When I turned 15, she gave me the original copy she had saved. I've read this book 3 times already. It is my absolute favorite. Desiree was the daughter of a merchant in France before Napoleon Bonaparte rose to power.   <span id="freeText13465570568070412745" style="display:none">My mother was reading this book when she was pregnant with me. When I turned 15, she gave me the original copy she had saved. I've read this book 3 times already. It is my absolute favorite. Desiree was the daughter of a merchant in France before Napoleon Bonaparte rose to power. The book explores Desiree's life and trials and how she falls in love with Napoleon. Love is not enough to keep these two together. As Napoleon emerges into a powerful leader, he must follow his path in order to succeed, and true love is sacrificed in order for him to follow his calling. Napoleon's rise and fall are explored in the book. Desiree later becomes Queen of Sweden but always keeps a fond place in her heart for her one true love. The book really took me back to that period and it is beautifully written by Selinko.</span>

<div id="review_2188689367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188689367" />
    <a title="AdiTurbo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2199883-aditurbo"><img alt="AdiTurbo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267856658p2/2199883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188689367?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AdiTurbo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AdiTurbo" href="/user/show/2199883-aditurbo">AdiTurbo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188689367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8868373182762497894">I enjoyed this book as a child, but trying to read it now only disappointed me. I didn't find in it the same magic that made it such a hit at the time. Now it feels very confused to me, with characters behaving in inconsistent ways and the plot jumping places and times and sometimes being practically incoherent. Selinko knew her history, but many times she focuses on details that are merely gossip, and are irrelevant in the bigger scheme of things. On the other hand, she takes it for granted tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8868373182762497894" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book as a child, but trying to read it now only disappointed me. I didn't find in it the same magic that made it such a hit at the time. Now it feels very confused to me, with characters behaving in inconsistent ways and the plot jumping places and times and sometimes being practically incoherent. Selinko knew her history, but many times she focuses on details that are merely gossip, and are irrelevant in the bigger scheme of things. On the other hand, she takes it for granted that her readers know enough about Napoleon, his politics and conquers, so that she skips on important issues and events that should be better explained. All in all, I don't think it's a well-written book, and is more romantic fluff than proper historical fiction. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8868373182762497894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2618253302?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/611105-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jennifer by: </span>
      Jennifer Payne
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618253302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6243094769310352567">Years ago, my team at work created a list of our own favorite, recommended books. (122 books total. I’ve read 65 of them now.) And JBP raved about this one. But because it was published in 1953, my local library did not have a copy. So I’d check every now and then just to make sure. And last month, a lasting memory paid off. <br/><br/>Though more than 60 years old, this book fits in beautifully with all this historical fiction these days that tells us the story through the perspective of the women. You mi</span>
  <span id="freeText6243094769310352567" style="display:none">Years ago, my team at work created a list of our own favorite, recommended books. (122 books total. I’ve read 65 of them now.) And JBP raved about this one. But because it was published in 1953, my local library did not have a copy. So I’d check every now and then just to make sure. And last month, a lasting memory paid off. <br /><br />Though more than 60 years old, this book fits in beautifully with all this historical fiction these days that tells us the story through the perspective of the women. You miss the battle scenes, but you get a better idea of the machinations behind the scenes. While this does have a bit of romance, it is more heavily-weighted to the historical. I learned a lot and went on a ton of Wikipedia adventures. <br /><br />How have I never heard of this woman before? Her descendants are still royalty in Sweden for Pete’s sake. It seems the more I read, the more I realize I don’t know. Gotta track down the movie version now. <br /><br />Thanks JBP for adding this to our favorites list. Another point for Jenn. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6243094769310352567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39130176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39130176" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1757501-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39130176?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" rel="nofollow" href="/user/show/1757501-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39130176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12004124186371362938">Historical fiction about Desiree' Clary, who was Napoleon Bonaparte's fiance before he married Josephine. This book is out of print, but one of my all time favorites (I'm a bit of a Napoleon fanatic). I won't give anything away, but the small but significant role that Desiree' played during a defining time in world history is amazing to me. There is also a movie staring Marlon Brando - but it's a waste of time!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5hC8ms6NYNocApxwqsfcASxxzsRwyvk3ilF5axnPQEUe17xvSJOtQM6adoRcfXrPpGLqx94/SEFCi5bGRwWNXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V1NFnK5HRgcGPQaejr3ZailuFd48RZlNPBIdLvRl9RWvlEVpKFmLndSl7Gp4B3+koX0x3ZKwKDv0yPKDqq84DA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

It is the tragic monologue of a woman speaking with the child she carries in her womb. This letter confronts the burning theme of abortion, and the meaning of life, by asking difficult questions: Is it fair to impose life even if it means suffering? Would it be better not to be born at all?\nLetter to a Child Never Born touches on the real meaning of being a woman: the power to give life or not. When the book begins, the protagonist is upset after learning she is pregnant. She knows nothing about the child, except that this creature depends totally and uniquely on her own choices. The creation of another person directly within one’s own body is a very shocking thing. The sense of responsibility is huge; it is a heavy burden that gives life to endless reflections, from the origin of our existence to the shame of our selfishness. If the child could choose, would he prefer to be born, to grow up, and to suffer, or would he return to the joyful limbo from which he came? A woman’s freedom and individuality are also challenged by a newborn—should she renounce her freedom, her job, and her choice? Apart from incidents in Egypt, the novel charts Sinuhe\'s travels in then Egyptian-dominated Syria, in Mitanni, Babylon, Minoan Crete, Mitanni, and among the Hittites.The main character of the novel is named after a character in an ancient Egyptian text commonly known as The Story of Sinuhe. The original story dates to a time long before that of Akhenaten: texts are known from as early as the 12th Dynasty.Much concerned about the historical accuracy of his detailed description of ancient Egyptian life forced the author to carry out considerable research into the subject. The result has been praised not only by readers but also by Egyptologists.Waltari had long been interested in Akhenaten and wrote a play about him which was staged in Helsinki in 1938. <span id="freeTextContainer16131483991949616129">Annemarie Selinko (September 1, 1914 - July 28, 1986) was an Austrian novelist who wrote a number of best-selling books in German from the 1930s through the 1950s. Although she had been based in Germany, in 1939 at the start of World War II she took refuge in Denmark with her Danish husband, but then in 1943, they again became refugees, this time to Sweden.<br/><br/>Many of her novels have been adapted into</span>
  <span id="freeText16131483991949616129" style="display:none">Annemarie Selinko (September 1, 1914 - July 28, 1986) was an Austrian novelist who wrote a number of best-selling books in German from the 1930s through the 1950s. Although she had been based in Germany, in 1939 at the start of World War II she took refuge in Denmark with her Danish husband, but then in 1943, they again became refugees, this time to Sweden.<br /><br />Many of her novels have been adapted into movies and all have been translated into numerous languages. Her last work Désirée (1951) was about Désirée Clary, one of Napoleon's lovers and, later, a queen of Sweden. It has been translated into 25 languages and in 1956 was turned into a movie with Marlon Brando and Jean Simmons. It is dedicated to her sister Liselotte, who was murdered by the Nazis.<br /><br />Bibliography<br /><br /> * Ich war ein häßliches Mädchen (I Was an Ugly Girl), Vienna: Kirschner Verlag, 1937; Made into a film, West Germany, 1955.<br /> * Morgen wird alles besser (Tomorrow is Always Better), 1941; Made into a film, Morgen gaat het beter, Netherlands, 1939<br /> * Heute heiratet mein Mann (My Husband Marries Today), 1943; Made into a film, West Germany, 1956.<br /> * Désirée, 1952; Made into a film, U.S., 1954.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16131483991949616129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
